I've seen folks use cuticle scissors all the way up to large fabric shears. I even saw someone use sheep-shearing scissors. NO shit. Oh, so many fails.   So, watching the video of the follower, she has a great pair of very sharp scissors. One and done. Brad, are you gluten intolerant? Oats are a big problem in the gluten-free community because a lot of them are contaminated by the way they're processed. Purity protocol oats are one of the few safe options out there, and I honestly don't think many of the oat milk companies use them right now. (I found about 2-3 on Google, but they're not any of the "mainstream" brands you'll see in the refrigerated section at the store.) You might try buying some purity protocol oats (I like Grainful) and making your own oat milk. Then, see if you have a reaction. :)

(Cashew cream recipe below) I don't know if you are gluten tolerant/intolerant/celiac, but there is a huge issue with oats being contaminated with wheat (gluten). Certified gluten free oats even often cause reactions in celiacs. Certain oat brands are more reliably gluten free than others, but I do recommend trying a few different brands of oat milk that are gluten free to see if it makes any difference for you (I just developed gluten intolerance when I was 25). You can also make you own gluten free oat milk (easily!!!). Low stomach acid can cause also cause intolerances (happened to me - but is treatable).  Best ever and easiest recipe for cashew cream (use for anything - coffee, soups, baking, etc):  Ingredients: - 2 cups filtered cold water - 1/2 raw/not-roasted unsalted cashews Instructions: No need to soak the cashews for this recipe (I have used this recipe many times). Blend in a high speed blender or magic bullet for 30 seconds to 1 minute (until the consistency is smooth and creamy, not grainy/chunky). Keep in fridge for up to 3 days.

RE Oatmilk allergy.  Get some antihistamines. A daily one like Claritin or Zyrtec and an emergency/quick acting one like Benadryl. Then look up elimination diets. Follow that for oats. Basically read all your ingredients lists to avoid anything with oats in it. Eliminate them from your diet for a few weeks and see if you notice a difference. Definitely keep a record so you notice any differences that are unexpected like headaches, sinus changes, rashes, etc.
